    <div id="node-90" class="node clear-block">


  <h2><a href="/rawmaintop" title=""></a></h2>

  <div class="meta">
  
    </div>

  <div class="content">
    <!--
--><!--
--><p><img id="top_bkground" src="http://southasia.berkeley.edu/sites/default/files/shared/img/SEC-strip.png" /></p>
<div id="strip">
<div id="secondary_menu"><a href="/about-us">ABOUT</a> | <a href="/mailing-list">JOIN</a> | <a href="/contactsdirections">CONTACT</a> | <a href="give-big-south-asia">SUPPORT</a> | <a href="https://www.facebook.com/pages/Center-for-South-Asia-Studies/76502306608"><img id="facebook_icon" src="/sites/default/files/shared/img/facebook.png" alt="facebook logo" width="25" height="25" align="absmiddle" /></a> &nbsp;</div>

<div class="panel-region-separator"></div><div class="panel-pane pane-node-title"  id="page_title">
  
  
  
  <div class="pane-content">
    Academic Chairs  </div>

  
  </div>
<div class="panel-region-separator"></div><div class="panel-pane pane-node-body"  id="secondary_page_main">
  
  
  
  <div class="pane-content">
    <div id="internal_menu"><p style="text-align: right;"><strong><a href="/what-we-do">WHAT WE DO</a> | <a href="/privately-funded-programs">PRIVATELY FUNDED PROGRAMS</a> | ISAS CHAIRS | <a href="/collaborators-partnerships">PARTNERSHIPS</a> | <a href="committees">COMMITTEES</a></strong><strong> | </strong><strong><a href="/isas-news">IN THE NEWS</a></strong></p></div><p><strong> </strong></p> <hr><p>&nbsp;</p><p>ISAS has successfully secured private and government funds to enhance South Asia studies at Berkeley. The&nbsp;<span style="font-size: 12px; background-color: #ffffff;">Institute</span>&nbsp;has raised money for four Academic Chairs.</p><p style="TEXT-ALIGN: center"><img src="/sites/default/files/resize/shared/Kundan10red1-75x98.jpg" width="75" height="98" style="float: right; border: 10px solid white;" /></p> <p><a href="http://tamil.berkeley.edu/tamil-chair"><strong>Chair in Tamil Studies</strong><br></a>The Chair in Tamil Studies was established in November 1997, with help from the academic and Tamil-American communities, to insure the continued teaching of Tamil language and literature in the United States and to encourage the use of state-of-the-art technology in the study of Tamil. The current chair-holder is <a href="http://tamil.berkeley.edu/tamil-chair/current-chairholder"><span style="text-decoration: underline;">George L. Hart</span></a>, Professor of Tamil, in the Department of South and Southeast Asian Studies.</p> <p><strong>Indo-American Community Chair in India Studies</strong><strong><br></strong>The Indo-American Community Chair in India Studies endowment was the result of a community-based campaign in 1990 and 1991. Helped significantly by the efforts of the Consul General of India in San Francisco, the Hon. Satinder K. Lambah, hundreds of members of the Indo-American community throughout California and the West made contributions to this endowment. The Chair was officially inaugurated with two brilliant guest lecturers in 1991-1992, by Nobel laureate physicist S. Chandrasekhar and former U.S. Ambassador to India John Kenneth Galbraith. In addition to Consul General Lambah, Ambassador Abid Hussain and UC Berkeley Chancellor Chang-lin Tien spoke at the Chair inaugural. Also during that year ISAS brought two short-term holders of the Chair to lecture for several weeks at Berkeley, legal scholar Upendra Baxi and sociologist André Beteille both from Delhi University. Since then the Chair has been held by economist Mrinal Datta Chaudhuri, political scientist Subrata Mitra, environmentalist Ramachandra Guha, political scientist Sudipto Kaviraj, literary critic Meenakshi Mukherjee and others. <a href="http://polisci.berkeley.edu/people/faculty/person_detail.php?person=228" target="_blank">Professor Pradeep Chhibber </a>was named Chair when he joined the UC Berkeley faculty in 2001.</p> <p><strong><a href="http://southasia.berkeley.edu/sarah-kailath-chair-memorial-lecture" target="_blank">Sarah Kailath Chair of India Studies</a><br></strong>The Sarah Kailath Chair of India Studies was established by Thomas Kailath, and Vinita and Narendra Gupta in honor of <a href="http://www.stanford.edu/%7Etkailath/"><span style="text-decoration: underline;">Dr. Kailath's wife, Sarah Kailath</span></a>, to enhance awareness and knowledge of issues relating to the Indian subcontinent. Further details about the chair and Sarah Kailath may be viewed <a href="http://southasia.berkeley.edu/sarah-kailath-chair-memorial-lecture" target="_blank">here</a>. The current Sarah Kailath Chair is Professor <a href="http://southasia.berkeley.edu/lawrence-cohen-0" target="_blank">Lawrence Cohen</a>, Chair,&nbsp;<span style="font-size: 12px; background-color: #ffffff;">Institute</span>&nbsp;for South Asia Studies and Professor, Anthropology and South Asian Studies. Professors Raka Ray, Robert P. Goldman and Thomas Metcalf previously held the Chair.</p> <p><strong><a href="/berkeley-pakistan-initiative">Quaid-i-Azam Chair in Pakistan Studies</a><br></strong>The Quaid-i-Azam Chair of Pakistan Studies - named for Mohammed Ali Jinnah, the leader who founded Pakistan, also known by the title, "Father of the Nation," or "Quaid-i-Azam" - was established in May 1999 with the help of the government of Pakistan to encourage increased knowledge of Pakistan in the United States and to help forge better ties between American academics and their counterparts in Pakistan. The Pakistan government's Ministry of Education provides the funds for the chair-holder’s salary and other expenses. The Quaid-i-Azam Chair of Pakistan Studies is designated for a visiting scholar. It was held by<strong> Dr. Tariq Rahman</strong> in 2004.</p>  </div>

  
  </div>
  </div>

  <h2><a href="/rawmaintop" title=""></a></h2>

  <div class="meta">
  
    </div>

  <div class="content">
    <!--

<div id="strip">
<div id="secondary_menu"><a href="/about-us">ABOUT</a> | <a href="/mailing-list">JOIN</a> | <a href="/contactsdirections">CONTACT</a> | <a href="give-big-south-asia">SUPPORT</a> | <a href="https://www.facebook.com/pages/Center-for-South-Asia-Studies/76502306608"><img id="facebook_icon" src="/sites/default/files/shared/img/facebook.png" alt="facebook logo" width="25" height="25" align="absmiddle" /></a> &nbsp;</div>

<div class="panel-region-separator"></div><div class="panel-pane pane-node-title"  id="page_title">
  
  
  
  <div class="pane-content">
    Amrit Kaur Ahluwalia Memorial Grant Program  </div>

  
  </div>
<div class="panel-region-separator"></div><div class="panel-pane pane-node-body"  id="secondary_page_main">
  
  
  
  <div class="pane-content">
    <H3>The 2010 Amrit Kaur Ahluwalia Memorial<BR>Dissertation Research Award</H3>
<H6>Award Details:</H6>
<P>These grants are designed to support dissertation research for Ph.D. candidates whose research focuses on Sikh or Punjabi studies. We encourage proposals from students of any discipline in the humanities or social sciences.</P>
<H6>Eligibility:</H6>
<P>Open to Ph.D. students in any stage of their doctoral program. Preference will be given to students who are conducting their research or writing their dissertation.</P>
<H6>Awards:</H6>
<P>Two awards of $1,000 each will be awarded</P>
<H6>Timeline:</H6>
<P>- January 28, 2011: All proposals due by close of business.<BR>- February 18, 2011: Fellowship awards announced.</P>
<H6>To Apply:</H6>
<P>Applicants should submit a statement of purpose outlining their dissertation research project. The statement of purpose should be 2-3 pages long and should include a summary of the research, contribution to current knowledge, methodology for carrying out the research, and describe specifically how the funds will be used.</P>
<P>In addition, please supply an estimated budget, a timeline, a recent CV, and two letters of reference (one must be from your current dissertation advisor).</P>
<P>Please send applications by email to: (preferred)<BR><A href="mailto:pkala@berkeley.edu">pkala@berkeley.edu</A><BR>Or by mail to:<BR>Ahluwalia Dissertation Research Award<BR>Center for South Asia Studies<BR>10 Stephens Hall<BR>University of California, Berkeley<BR>Berkeley, CA 94720</P>
<P>For further information please contact:<BR>Center for South Asia Studies<BR><A href="mailto:csas@berkeley.edu">csas@berkeley.edu</A><BR>510-642-3608</P>  </div>

  
  </div>
  </div>

<div class="panel-region-separator"></div><div class="panel-pane pane-node-body"  id="secondary_page_main">
  
  
  
  <div class="pane-content">
    <p style="text-align: right;"><span style="font-size: 12px; background-color: #ffffff;"><span style="background-color: #ffffff;"><span style="font-size: 12px; background-color: #ffffff;"><a href="http://southasia.berkeley.edu/bhattacharya-india-fund" style="background-color: #ffffff;">Program</a><span style="background-color: #ffffff; font-size: 12px;">&nbsp;|&nbsp;</span><a href="http://southasia.berkeley.edu/bhattacharya-lectureship" style="background-color: #ffffff;">Lectureship</a><span style="background-color: #ffffff; font-size: 12px;">&nbsp;|&nbsp;</span><span style="background-color: #ffffff; font-size: 12px;"><a href="http://southasia.berkeley.edu/bhattacharya-graduate-fellowship">Graduate Fellowship</a></span>&nbsp;|</span><span style="font-size: 12px; background-color: #ffffff; line-height: 1.5em;">&nbsp;</span>Awardees</span></span></p><hr><p><span style="font-size: 12px;">The Bhattacharya Graduate Fellowship</span>&nbsp;provides support for graduate fellowships in the form of competitive grants of up to<span style="background-color: #ffffff; font-size: 12px; line-height: 1.5em;">&nbsp;$1000 for research travel to&nbsp;</span><span style="background-color: #ffffff; font-size: 12px; line-height: 1.5em;">S</span><span style="background-color: #ffffff; font-size: 12px; line-height: 1.5em;">outh Asia (two will be awarded) and $500 for domestic conference travel or in-country library research (two will be awarded)</span><span style="font-size: 12px; line-height: 1.5em;">. For further details on the application procedure and deadlines, please click&nbsp;</span><a href="http://southasia.berkeley.edu/bhattacharya-graduate-fellowship">here</a><span style="font-size: 12px; line-height: 1.5em;">.</span></p><h4><strong style="font-size: 12.800000190734863px;">Awardees</strong></h4><table border="0"><tbody><tr><td style="border-width: 1px; border-style: solid;" rowspan="5">2017</td><td style="border-width: 1px; border-style: solid;" rowspan="2"><strong>Research</strong></td><td style="border-width: 1px; border-style: solid;">Bhumi Purohit (PhD candidate, Political Science, UC Berkeley)<br><strong>Information and Political Polarization: Can Policy Data Reduce Ethnically and Religiously Polarizing Rhetoric in Indian Political Campaigns?</strong><br></td></tr><tr><td style="border-width: 1px; border-style: solid;">Anirvan Chowdhury (PhD candidate, Political Science, UC Berkeley)<br><strong>Consolidating power after hegemons decline: evidence from West Bengal, India</strong></td></tr><tr><td style="border-width: 1px; border-style: solid;" rowspan="3"><strong style="font-size: 12px; background-color: #ffffff;">Conference</strong></td><td style="border-width: 1px; border-style: solid;">Lisa Brooks (PhD candidate, South and Southeast Asian Studies, UC Berkeley)<br><strong>Fluid Bodies: Leeches in Classical&nbsp;<span style="font-size: 12px;">Āyurvedic Medical Compendia and Practice</span></strong></td></tr><tr><td>Shakthi Nataraj (PhD candidate, Anthropology, UC Berkeley)<br><strong>A mother, a man, and an anthropologist</strong></td></tr><tr><td style="border-width: 1px; border-style: solid;">William F Stafford Jr (PhD candidate, Anthropology, UC Berkeley)<br><strong>Value and the Distribution of Proximity: The Autorickshaw Meter and Regimes of Location</strong><br></td></tr></tbody></table>  </div>

  
  </div>

    <div id="node-90" class="node clear-block">


  <h2><a href="/rawmaintop" title=""></a></h2>

  <div class="meta">
  
    </div>

  <div class="content">
    <!--
--><!--
--><p><img id="top_bkground" src="http://southasia.berkeley.edu/sites/default/files/shared/img/SEC-strip.png" /></p>
<div id="strip">
<div id="secondary_menu"><a href="/about-us">ABOUT</a> | <a href="/mailing-list">JOIN</a> | <a href="/contactsdirections">CONTACT</a> | <a href="give-big-south-asia">SUPPORT</a> | <a href="https://www.facebook.com/pages/Center-for-South-Asia-Studies/76502306608"><img id="facebook_icon" src="/sites/default/files/shared/img/facebook.png" alt="facebook logo" width="25" height="25" align="absmiddle" /></a> &nbsp;</div>

<div class="panel-region-separator"></div><div class="panel-pane pane-node-title"  id="page_title">
  
  
  
  <div class="pane-content">
    Bhattacharya Graduate Fellowship  </div>

  
  </div>
<div class="panel-region-separator"></div><div class="panel-pane pane-node-body"  id="secondary_page_main">
  
  
  
  <div class="pane-content">
    <p style="text-align: right;"><a href="http://southasia.berkeley.edu/bhattacharya-india-fund">Program</a>&nbsp;| <a href="http://southasia.berkeley.edu/bhattacharya-lectureship">Lectureship</a> | <span style="font-size: 12px; background-color: #ffffff;">Graduate Fellowship&nbsp;</span><span style="background-color: #ffffff; font-size: 12px;">|&nbsp;</span><span style="font-size: 12px; background-color: #ffffff;"><a href="http://southasia.berkeley.edu/bhattacharya-graduate-fellows">Awardees</a></span></p><hr><p><a href="http://southasia.berkeley.edu/bhattacharya-graduate-fellowship-awardees" style="background-color: #ffffff; text-decoration: underline;"><img src="https://southasia.berkeley.edu/sites/default/files/resize/shared/Bhattacharya/Bhattacharya_Awardees-178x178.png" width="178" height="178" style="float: right;" /></a></p><p><span style="font-size: 12px; background-color: #ffffff;">The&nbsp;</span><a href="http://southasia.berkeley.edu/bhattacharya-graduate-fellowship" style="background-color: #ffffff;">Bhattacharya Graduate Fellowship</a><span style="font-size: 12px; background-color: #ffffff;">&nbsp;will award UC Berkeley graduate students competitive grants for</span><span style="background-color: #ffffff; font-size: 12px;">&nbsp;topics related to contemporary India&nbsp;</span><span style="background-color: #ffffff; font-size: 12px;">of up to</span></p><ol><li>$1000 for research travel to India (a total of two will be awarded) and&nbsp;</li><li>$500 for domestic conference travel for presentations (a total of four will be awarded).</li></ol><p>The application process will&nbsp;<strong>open</strong>&nbsp;on February 1, 2018<span style="font-size: 12px; background-color: #ffffff;">&nbsp;for travel or conferences to take place during the summer of 2018 (i.e., May through August 2018) or the 2018-19 academic year (i.e. August 2018 through May 2019). </span></p><p><span style="font-size: 12px; background-color: #ffffff;"><strong>D</strong></span><strong style="background-color: #ffffff; font-size: 12px;">eadline</strong><span style="background-color: #ffffff; font-size: 12px;">&nbsp;for submission of application materials</span><span style="font-size: 12px; background-color: #ffffff;">&nbsp;is&nbsp;</span><strong style="font-size: 12px; background-color: #ffffff;">April 15, 2018</strong><span style="font-size: 12px; background-color: #ffffff;">&nbsp;by</span><strong style="font-size: 12px; background-color: #ffffff;">&nbsp;5 pm</strong><span style="font-size: 12px; background-color: #ffffff;">.</span></p><p><strong>Open only to UC Berkeley graduate students.&nbsp;</strong></p><p>Please submit your application by using the application portals listed below.&nbsp;</p><table border="0"><tbody><tr><td class="table_background" style="width: 50%; border: 1px solid #8b8a74; text-align: center;" colspan="2"><strong>Before starting your application, please make sure to have the following documents ready.<br></strong></td></tr><tr><td style="border: 1px solid #8b8a74;"><p><strong style="font-size: 12px; text-align: center;"><a href="https://tango.berkeley.edu/applicant/app/tangoCreateApplicant?programId=1218&amp;cycleId=221" target="_blank" style="text-decoration: underline;">APPLICATION PORTAL FOR RESEARCH TRAVEL</a><br><span style="color: #ff0000;">Deadline:&nbsp;</span></strong><strong style="font-size: 12px; text-align: center;"><strong style="font-size: 12px; text-align: center;"><span style="font-size: 12px;"><span style="color: #ff0000;">April 15, 2018 by 5 PM</span></span></strong></strong></p></td><td style="border: 1px solid #8b8a74;"><p><strong style="font-size: 12px; text-align: center;"><a href="https://tango.berkeley.edu/applicant/app/tangoCreateApplicant?programId=1232&amp;cycleId=221" target="_blank">APPLICATION PORTAL FOR CONFERENCE TRAVEL</a><br><strong style="font-size: 12px; text-align: center;"><span style="font-size: 12px;"><span style="color: #ff0000;">Deadline: April 15, 2018 by 5 PM</span></span></strong></strong></p></td></tr><tr><td style="border: 1px solid #8b8a74;"><p style="color: #333333;">In your application for I<strong>N-COUNTRY LIBRARY</strong> or <strong>RESEARCH</strong> <strong>TRAVEL</strong>, please include the following:</p><ol style="font-size: 15.2px; color: #333333; font-family: Verdana, Arial, Helvetica, sans-serif;"><li>A cover letter stating the need for travel (750 words or less)</li><li>A 2-page project proposal (double-spaced) (PDF format)</li><li>A budget (only for research) (PDF format)</li><li>A CV (PDF format)</li><li>One letter of support from your advisor (PDF, sent by the recommenders directly)</li><li>Please Note:<ul style="font-size: 12px;"><li>One award of upto $500 will be given for In-Country Library Research</li><li>Two awards of upto $1000 each will be given for Research Travel to South Asia</li></ul></li></ol></td><td style="border: 1px solid #8b8a74;"><p style="color: #333333;"><span style="font-size: 12px;"><strong>CONFERENCE TRAVEL</strong></span>&nbsp;is only available for presenting your own research. In your application for conference travel, please include:</p><ol style="font-size: 15.2px; color: #333333; font-family: Verdana, Arial, Helvetica, sans-serif;"><li>A cover letter with information of the conference (500 words or less)</li><li>If available, a print out or copy of the conference schedule showing your presentation listing (PDF format)</li><li>An abstract of your presentation (PDF format)</li><li>A CV (PDF format)</li><li>Please Note:<ul style="font-size: 12px;"><li>Applicants may apply before their panels/papers are accepted. Disbursement of the money will be conditional on acceptance of paper by a panel/conference.</li><li>Awardees will be reimbursed up to $500 of their travel expenses upon presentation of copies of air-tickets/panel registration forms.</li></ul></li></ol></td></tr><tr><td class="table_background" style="border: 1px solid #8b8a74;" colspan="2"><p style="color: #333333; text-align: center;"><strong>Please submit applications through the application portals provided above. Emailed applications will not be accepted.<br><span style="font-size: 12px;">For questions, please email:&nbsp;</span><span style="font-size: 12px; color: #000000;">Puneeta Kala at&nbsp;</span><a href="mailto:pkala@berkeley.edu">pkala@berkeley.edu</a></strong></p></td></tr></tbody></table>  </div>

  
  </div>
  </div>
</div>
  </div>

<div class="panel-region-separator"></div><div class="panel-pane pane-node-title"  id="page_title">
  
  
  
  <div class="pane-content">
    Bhattacharya Graduate Fellowship Awardees  </div>

  
  </div>
<div class="panel-region-separator"></div><div class="panel-pane pane-node-body"  id="secondary_page_main">
  
  
  
  <div class="pane-content">
    <p style="text-align: right;"><a href="http://southasia.berkeley.edu/bhattacharya-india-fund">Program</a>&nbsp;| <a href="http://southasia.berkeley.edu/bhattacharya-lectureship">Lectureship</a> | <span style="font-size: 12px; background-color: #ffffff;"><a href="http://southasia.berkeley.edu/bhattacharya-graduate-fellowship">Graduate Fellowship</a></span></p><hr><p><span style="background-color: #ffffff; font-size: 12px;">The&nbsp;</span><a href="http://southasia.berkeley.edu/bhattacharya-graduate-fellowship" style="background-color: #ffffff;">Bhattacharya Graduate Fellowship</a><span style="background-color: #ffffff; font-size: 12px;">&nbsp;will award graduate students competitive grants for research travel to India and up to $500 for domestic conference travel for presentations on topics related to contemporary India. </span>&nbsp;For further details on the application procedure and deadlines,  please click <a href="http://southasia.berkeley.edu/bhattacharya-graduate-fellowship">here</a>.</p><h4><strong>Awardees</strong></h4><table border="0"><tbody><tr><td style="border-width: 1px; border-style: solid;" rowspan="2">2017</td><td style="border-width: 1px; border-style: solid;"><strong>Research</strong></td><td style="border-width: 1px; border-style: solid;"><strong><br></strong></td></tr><tr><td style="border-width: 1px; border-style: solid;"><strong>Conference</strong></td><td style="border-width: 1px; border-style: solid;"><strong><br></strong></td></tr></tbody></table>  </div>

<div class="panel-region-separator"></div><div class="panel-pane pane-node-title"  id="page_title">
  
  
  
  <div class="pane-content">
    Fulbright Reentry Seminar 2016  </div>

  
  </div>
<div class="panel-region-separator"></div><div class="panel-pane pane-node-body"  id="secondary_page_main">
  
  
  
  <div class="pane-content">
    <p style="text-align: right;"><span style="font-size: 12px; background-color: #ffffff;">home &nbsp; |&nbsp;&nbsp;</span><a href="http://southasia.berkeley.edu/collecting-south-asia" target="_blank" style="line-height: 18px; background-color: #ffffff;">&nbsp;</a><span style="background-color: #ffffff;"><a href="http://southasia.berkeley.edu/sites/default/files/shared/events/Fulbright_2016/Fulbright_PDO_2016.pdf" target="_blank">agenda</a></span><span style="font-size: 12px; background-color: #ffffff;">&nbsp;&nbsp; | &nbsp; &nbsp;</span><span style="background-color: #ffffff;"><a href="http://southasia.berkeley.edu/speakers-3">speakers</a></span><span style="font-size: 12px; background-color: #ffffff;">&nbsp;&nbsp; | &nbsp;&nbsp;</span><span style="background-color: #ffffff;"><a href="http://southasia.berkeley.edu/fulbright-student-list">participants</a></span><span style="font-size: 12px; line-height: 1.5em; background-color: #ffffff;">&nbsp;&nbsp; | &nbsp; <a href="http://southasia.berkeley.edu/success-stories">success stories</a>&nbsp;&nbsp;</span><span style="font-size: 12px; background-color: #ffffff;">| &nbsp; <a href="http://southasia.berkeley.edu/photos">photos</a>&nbsp;</span><span style="font-size: 12px; background-color: #ffffff;">&nbsp;</span><span style="font-size: 12px; line-height: 1.5em; background-color: #ffffff;">|</span><span style="font-size: 12px; background-color: #ffffff;">&nbsp; &nbsp;<a href="http://southasia.berkeley.edu/resources-0">resources</a> &nbsp;|</span><span style="font-size: 12px; line-height: 1.5em; background-color: #ffffff;">&nbsp;&nbsp;</span><a href="http://southasia.berkeley.edu/contactsdirections" target="_blank" style="line-height: 18px; background-color: #ffffff;">contact</a></p><hr><p><em style="font-size: 12px; line-height: 1.5em;">(Please click on the red text below for links to short video clips from the four day seminar. The photo on the right features some students who visited the Institute.)</em></p><p><span style="font-size: 12px; line-height: 1.5em;"><img src="https://southasia.berkeley.edu/sites/default/files/resize/shared/events/Fulbright_2016/in_ISAS-400x231.png" width="400" height="231" style="float: right; margin-left: 15px; margin-bottom: 10px;" /></span></p><p>In April 2016, the Institute for South Asia Studies at UC Berkeley was awarded a grant from the Institute of International Education and the Department of State's Bureau of Educational and Cultural Affairs to host the 2016 Fulbright Pakistan Social Entrepreneurship and Re-entry Seminar. After months of organizing, the ISAS hosted 130 Pakistani students for a four-day seminar from April 27 – May 1. This seminar (full agenda can be found <a href="http://southasia.berkeley.edu/sites/default/files/shared/events/Fulbright_2016/Fulbright_PDO_2016.pdf">HERE</a>) prepared the students for their return home and introduced them to the field of social enterprise.</p><p>The welcoming dinner at the Oakland Marriott City Center began with remarks from <a href="https://youtu.be/QGbOMVuKZZ4" onclick="window.open('https://youtu.be/QGbOMVuKZZ4','','width=600,height=700,left='+(screen.availWidth/2-300)+',top='+(screen.availHeight/2-350)+'');return false;">MUNIS FARUQUI</a>, Professor in the Dept of SSEAS and Co-Chair of the Berkeley Pakistan Initiative. Welcoming the students to Berkeley, Professor Faruqui spoke about the history of the Berkeley Pakistan Initiative and introduced the next set of speakers. <a href="https://youtu.be/lX1cUKmJy5Y" onclick="window.open('https://youtu.be/lX1cUKmJy5Y','','width=600,height=700,left='+(screen.availWidth/2-300)+',top='+(screen.availHeight/2-350)+'');return false;">DAVID RANZ</a> from the Department of State congratulated the students on the completion of their Fulbright programs. <a href="https://youtu.be/Z-px2z0cSa0" onclick="window.open('https://youtu.be/Z-px2z0cSa0','','width=600,height=700,left='+(screen.availWidth/2-300)+',top='+(screen.availHeight/2-350)+'');return false;">AMBASSADOR JILANI</a> to the U.S. from the Islamic Republic of Pakistan reminded the students of the immense impact that they could make in Pakistan because of this program. The evening keynote speaker was <a href="https://youtu.be/e9k1XzLknck" onclick="window.open('https://youtu.be/e9k1XzLknck','','width=600,height=700,left='+(screen.availWidth/2-300)+',top='+(screen.availHeight/2-350)+'');return false;">AMRA TAREEN</a>, the President of Organization of Pakistani Entrepreneurs (OPEN) Silicon Valley. Speaking from her own experience in enterprise, Amra delivered an inspiring lecture and encouraged the students to use their passions and interests to contribute to Pakistan.</p><p>Following a successful opening dinner, the students were connected the next day via Skype to twelve Pakistani Fulbright alumni. This <a href="https://youtu.be/5ZCa1562T1k" onclick="window.open('https://youtu.be/5ZCa1562T1k','','width=600,height=700,left='+(screen.availWidth/2-300)+',top='+(screen.availHeight/2-350)+'');return false;">VIRTUAL ALUMNI PANEL</a> provided the students with an opportunity to hear how the alumni used their degrees to further their professional career and how they navigated their return to Pakistan. After the panel, the U.S. Educational Foundation in Pakistan showed videos of Fulbright alumni that had actually started social enterprises in Pakistan such as <a href="https://youtu.be/PReYLuuYElk" onclick="window.open('https://youtu.be/PReYLuuYElk','','width=600,height=700,left='+(screen.availWidth/2-300)+',top='+(screen.availHeight/2-350)+'');return false;">BUSHRA RAHIM</a> and <a href="https://youtu.be/ynv86sevP8Y" onclick="window.open('https://youtu.be/ynv86sevP8Y','','width=600,height=700,left='+(screen.availWidth/2-300)+',top='+(screen.availHeight/2-350)+'');return false;">OMAR ADNAN</a>. These videos showed the potential that these Fulbright students have to make change in Pakistan.</p><p>Many of these 130 students had never met each other before. Coming from different institutions across the US and from a diverse range of disciplines, this was the first time that many of them were meeting their fellow Fulbrighters. <a href="https://youtu.be/Shv7n9JWlsE" onclick="window.open('https://youtu.be/Shv7n9JWlsE','','width=600,height=700,left='+(screen.availWidth/2-300)+',top='+(screen.availHeight/2-350)+'');return false;">SANCHITA SAXENA</a>, Executive Director of the ISAS, broke the ice and had the students introduce themselves to someone new through a game. This allowed the students to break away from their discipline and meet others from different universities. Further contributing to this interdisciplinary space was <a href="https://youtu.be/EBLlYCZT4ZY" onclick="window.open('https://youtu.be/EBLlYCZT4ZY','','width=600,height=700,left='+(screen.availWidth/2-300)+',top='+(screen.availHeight/2-350)+'');return false;">TATHEER HAMDANI</a> from Habib University who spoke to the students about the interdisciplinary space that Habib University is striving to provide in Karachi.</p><p>The students then began a workshop that aimed to help them navigate their return to Pakistan. Led by Jason Patent, Jess Delegencia, and Lauren Moloney-Egnatios from the <a href="https://youtu.be/I7Py6vK56PA" onclick="window.open('https://youtu.be/I7Py6vK56PA','','width=600,height=700,left='+(screen.availWidth/2-300)+',top='+(screen.availHeight/2-350)+'');return false;">CENTER FOR INTERCULTURAL LEADERSHIP</a> at UC Berkeley, this workshop provided students with the opportunities to integrate what they had learned in the US with their life at home and to their future career decisions. This session provided the students with the opportunity to create a supportive community. Students such as <a href="https://youtu.be/AGmmnbry-Bg" onclick="window.open('https://youtu.be/AGmmnbry-Bg','','width=600,height=700,left='+(screen.availWidth/2-300)+',top='+(screen.availHeight/2-350)+'');return false;">SARAH HUSSAIN</a> and <a href="https://youtu.be/D9v345Hs6d4" onclick="window.open('https://youtu.be/D9v345Hs6d4','','width=600,height=700,left='+(screen.availWidth/2-300)+',top='+(screen.availHeight/2-350)+'');return false;">MADIHA PARVEZ</a> used this opportunity to reflect on their time in the US and share their perspective on how they would use the Fulbright experience to contribute to Pakistan. <a href="https://youtu.be/VnOKAU1k3x0" onclick="window.open('https://youtu.be/VnOKAU1k3x0','','width=600,height=700,left='+(screen.availWidth/2-300)+',top='+(screen.availHeight/2-350)+'');return false;">DILAWAR SYED</a>, President of Freshdesk and OPEN Global, continued the theme of civic innovation in Pakistan during his evening keynote lecture. Drawing from his experiences in Sialkot and with the White House, Dilawar provided examples of how the students could impact Pakistan.</p><p>Recognizing the power and privileges of the Fulbright program was a significant theme during this seminar. In an engaging workshop on Friday morning, Dean <a href="https://youtu.be/QNL6Tr7n0Q0" onclick="window.open('https://youtu.be/QNL6Tr7n0Q0','','width=600,height=700,left='+(screen.availWidth/2-300)+',top='+(screen.availHeight/2-350)+'');return false;">SUDHA SHETTY</a> taught participants how to map their own individual power and networks. After students realized their own resources, she then had them work in interdisciplinary groups to address issues such as <a href="https://youtu.be/ytNnGXTeSFs" onclick="window.open('https://youtu.be/ytNnGXTeSFs','','width=600,height=700,left='+(screen.availWidth/2-300)+',top='+(screen.availHeight/2-350)+'');return false;">PROMOTING WOMEN IN STEM</a>&nbsp;and <a href="https://youtu.be/9_MEDCpnxR4" onclick="window.open('https://youtu.be/9_MEDCpnxR4','','width=600,height=700,left='+(screen.availWidth/2-300)+',top='+(screen.availHeight/2-350)+'');return false;">CHILDREN’S EDUCATION</a>. This workshop prepared the students to begin thinking about how they could all become social entrepreneurs by using their existing talents.</p><p>The remainder of the day focused on social enterprise and began with a <a href="https://youtu.be/LqIyMFa7oOw" onclick="window.open('https://youtu.be/LqIyMFa7oOw','','width=600,height=700,left='+(screen.availWidth/2-300)+',top='+(screen.availHeight/2-350)+'');return false;">PANEL</a> on social enterprise. <a href="https://youtu.be/w0-jPpy_xvc" onclick="window.open('https://youtu.be/w0-jPpy_xvc','','width=600,height=700,left='+(screen.availWidth/2-300)+',top='+(screen.availHeight/2-350)+'');return false;">GEORGE SCHARFFENBERGER</a> from UC Berkeley provided an introduction to social enterprise while <a href="https://youtu.be/rjy7ifDAQQE" onclick="window.open('https://youtu.be/rjy7ifDAQQE','','width=600,height=700,left='+(screen.availWidth/2-300)+',top='+(screen.availHeight/2-350)+'');return false;">RICHARD MARTINEZ</a>, <a href="https://youtu.be/Qi7f_4rTHdg" onclick="window.open('https://youtu.be/Qi7f_4rTHdg','','width=600,height=700,left='+(screen.availWidth/2-300)+',top='+(screen.availHeight/2-350)+'');return false;">CHAD STERBENZ</a>, and <a href="https://youtu.be/vIMhJ3BGzuo" onclick="window.open('https://youtu.be/vIMhJ3BGzuo','','width=600,height=700,left='+(screen.availWidth/2-300)+',top='+(screen.availHeight/2-350)+'');return false;">ASIM FAYAZ</a> all provided insights from their own social enterprises. <a href="https://youtu.be/MzjdUYPWCN4" onclick="window.open('https://youtu.be/MzjdUYPWCN4','','width=600,height=700,left='+(screen.availWidth/2-300)+',top='+(screen.availHeight/2-350)+'');return false;">UMAR AKRAM</a>, a Cal student, gave an example of a social enterprise that was started by Pakistani students at Berkeley but seeks to improve maternal care in Pakistan.</p><p>After hearing about the theory of social enterprise, the Fulbrighters then split into various groups to visit social enterprises located in the Bay Area. These social enterprises worked on a diverse group of issues from working on affordable solar energy, providing <a href="https://youtu.be/MfYhbktX604" onclick="window.open('https://youtu.be/MfYhbktX604','','width=600,height=700,left='+(screen.availWidth/2-300)+',top='+(screen.availHeight/2-350)+'');return false;">VOCATIONAL TRAINING</a>&nbsp;for substance abusers and convicted criminals or using the power of film to market your social innovation. The day then culminated in a trip to Fisherman’s Wharf and dinner at two iconic San Francisco restaurants, Hard Rock Café and Bubba Gump.</p><p>On the final day of the seminar, the Fulbright students were invited to attend the annual forum held by the Silicon Valley chapter of <a href="https://youtu.be/cdT2Ou8foOs" onclick="window.open('https://youtu.be/cdT2Ou8foOs','','width=600,height=700,left='+(screen.availWidth/2-300)+',top='+(screen.availHeight/2-350)+'');return false;">OPEN</a>. At the forum, students were able to hear from successful entrepreneurs on a range of topics from <a href="https://youtu.be/1S3Kd7TG6H4" onclick="window.open('https://youtu.be/1S3Kd7TG6H4','','width=600,height=700,left='+(screen.availWidth/2-300)+',top='+(screen.availHeight/2-350)+'');return false;">McDONALD’S MARKETING STRATEGY</a>&nbsp;to <a href="https://youtu.be/Sdw9FD1im1Q" onclick="window.open('https://youtu.be/Sdw9FD1im1Q','','width=600,height=700,left='+(screen.availWidth/2-300)+',top='+(screen.availHeight/2-350)+'');return false;">PANORAMIC VIDEOS</a>. It also provided the students with <a href="https://youtu.be/JZ4DkFtyiJc" onclick="window.open('https://youtu.be/JZ4DkFtyiJc','','width=600,height=700,left='+(screen.availWidth/2-300)+',top='+(screen.availHeight/2-350)+'');return false;">UNPARALLELED NETWORKING OPPORTUNITIES</a>&nbsp;as one student successfully distributed over thirty business cards. Additional photos from the forum can be found <a href="https://photos.google.com/u/0/share/AF1QipPaHcHK53vC42BQwxr4n6773jj-Z2aaqfYAPLjx-b5p0DrczrmIlLTWeHRq6qEnHw?key=dXlYdVlCakc0eVRXWlRVWlJoelJuZlFnQ1o4aWVB" target="_blank">here</a>.</p><p>All 130 students came together at the Oakland Marriott for the final closing dinner. Welcoming the students and congratulating them on the completion of their Fulbright program was <a href="https://youtu.be/rS1VQs1YeA0" onclick="window.open('https://youtu.be/rS1VQs1YeA0','','width=600,height=700,left='+(screen.availWidth/2-300)+',top='+(screen.availHeight/2-350)+'');return false;">LAWRENCE COHEN</a>, Director of the ISAS. The students then had a chance to reflect on the last few days and to share their <a href="https://youtu.be/2PGJQDuW2FU" onclick="window.open('https://youtu.be/2PGJQDuW2FU','','width=600,height=700,left='+(screen.availWidth/2-300)+',top='+(screen.availHeight/2-350)+'');return false;">HOPES</a>&nbsp;and ideas for the future. It was extremely inspiring to see that after a short four days the students came together to support each other in various ideas such as promoting <a href="https://youtu.be/hRAkVIZ6MKE" onclick="window.open('https://youtu.be/hRAkVIZ6MKE','','width=600,height=700,left='+(screen.availWidth/2-300)+',top='+(screen.availHeight/2-350)+'');return false;">HIGHER EDUCATION IN GILGIT</a>, providing deaf/mute children with <a href="https://youtu.be/TxrHeIlnyz4" onclick="window.open('https://youtu.be/TxrHeIlnyz4','','width=600,height=700,left='+(screen.availWidth/2-300)+',top='+(screen.availHeight/2-350)+'');return false;">ACCESS TO EDUCATIONAL RESOURCES</a>, <a href="https://youtu.be/2N1KSMDtjcM" onclick="window.open('https://youtu.be/2N1KSMDtjcM','','width=600,height=700,left='+(screen.availWidth/2-300)+',top='+(screen.availHeight/2-350)+'');return false;">MAKING ROAD SIGNS ACCESSIBLE</a> to the blind, <a href="https://youtu.be/P2QSHqJPDHs" onclick="window.open('https://youtu.be/P2QSHqJPDHs','','width=600,height=700,left='+(screen.availWidth/2-300)+',top='+(screen.availHeight/2-350)+'');return false;">REBRANDING PAKISTAN</a>, and an app to provide <a href="https://youtu.be/qXuX7Fgz77c" onclick="window.open('https://youtu.be/qXuX7Fgz77c','','width=600,height=700,left='+(screen.availWidth/2-300)+',top='+(screen.availHeight/2-350)+'');return false;">HEALTH CARE</a> access to remote areas of Pakistan. Led by <a href="https://youtu.be/_6moPSvb33E" onclick="window.open('https://youtu.be/_6moPSvb33E','','width=600,height=700,left='+(screen.availWidth/2-300)+',top='+(screen.availHeight/2-350)+'');return false;">ASIM FAYAZ</a>, this session was truly amazing and a testament to how passionate and brilliant these students are. The final speech provided by <a href="https://youtu.be/TpxibTzjWz4" onclick="window.open('https://youtu.be/TpxibTzjWz4','','width=600,height=700,left='+(screen.availWidth/2-300)+',top='+(screen.availHeight/2-350)+'');return false;">BROOKE PEARSON</a> from the Department of State allowed the students to reflect on how the Fulbright program means more than just an education but it is also a means to create social impact in the world. The night ended with two Fulbright students <a href="https://youtu.be/0iL3TLpKxro" onclick="window.open('https://youtu.be/0iL3TLpKxro','','width=600,height=700,left='+(screen.availWidth/2-300)+',top='+(screen.availHeight/2-350)+'');return false;">THANKING</a> the Institute of International Education for providing them with the opportunity to be in the program.</p><p>This seminar was an incredible opportunity for the Institute for South Asia Studies to not only strengthen existing connections but to expand our network to incorporate a brilliant group of Pakistani students. We look forward to the possibility of hosting other such orientations and to working with the Institute of International Education and Department of State's&nbsp;<span style="font-size: 12px; background-color: #ffffff;">Bureau of Educational and Cultural Affairs</span><span style="font-size: 12px; line-height: 1.5em;">&nbsp;further!</span></p>  </div>

  
  </div>

  <h2><a href="/rawmaintop" title=""></a></h2>

  <div class="meta">
  
    </div>

  <div class="content">
    <!--
--><!--
--><p><img id="top_bkground" src="http://southasia.berkeley.edu/sites/default/files/shared/img/SEC-strip.png" /></p>
<div id="strip">
<div id="secondary_menu"><a href="/about-us">ABOUT</a> | <a href="/mailing-list">JOIN</a> | <a href="/contactsdirections">CONTACT</a> | <a href="give-big-south-asia">SUPPORT</a> | <a href="https://www.facebook.com/pages/Center-for-South-Asia-Studies/76502306608"><img id="facebook_icon" src="/sites/default/files/shared/img/facebook.png" alt="facebook logo" width="25" height="25" align="absmiddle" /></a> &nbsp;</div>

<div class="panel-region-separator"></div><div class="panel-pane pane-node-title"  id="page_title">
  
  
  
  <div class="pane-content">
    ISAS Visiting Scholars Program  </div>

  
  </div>
<div class="panel-region-separator"></div><div class="panel-pane pane-node-body"  id="secondary_page_main">
  
  
  
  <div class="pane-content">
    <p>&nbsp;</p><ul><li><strong><a href="#Criteria">Selection Criteria</a></strong></li><li><a href="#Review"><strong>Application Review</strong></a></li><li><a href="#Privileges"><strong>Privileges and Responsibilities of a Visiting Scholar</strong></a></li><li><a href="#Procedures"><strong>Application Procedures</strong></a></li><li><a href="#Fees"><strong>Fees</strong></a></li><li><strong><a href="http://southasia.berkeley.edu/people/visiting">Current ISAS Visiting Scholars</a></strong></li></ul><hr><h4><strong><a name="Criteria"></a>Selection Criteria</strong></h4><p>The Institute accepts visiting scholars who are pursuing a research project on South Asia that is transnational, border-crossing, or comparative in nature. We welcome&nbsp; applications from active academic researchers and university faculty members. Applicants are expected to hold advanced academic degrees. Special consideration will be given to applications with a research focus on one of our three current initatives: 1) Urdu and Pakistan studies, 2) South Asian contemporary art, 3) the Indian City. For more details about our current initiatives, please go to our Research Initiatives page <a href="http://southasia.berkeley.edu/isas-initiatives">here</a>. The Institute also welcomes applications from individuals with experience in government service, business or professional fields who are likely to benefit from interactions with research scholars. Current PhD students may apply for affiliation as a Visiting Student Researcher. These opportunities however are limited and are offered only in connection with current&nbsp;<span style="font-size: 12px; background-color: #ffffff;">Institute</span>&nbsp;initiatives or research projects. Furthermore, each visiting scholar must be nominated by a UC Berkeley faculty member.</p><h4><strong><a name="Review"></a>Application Review</strong></h4><p>The&nbsp;<span style="font-size: 12px; background-color: #ffffff;">Institute</span>&nbsp;for South Asia Studies reviews applications for visiting scholars three times a year.&nbsp;</p><ul><li>For arrival during the Fall Semester (August 15 – December) - <strong>DEADLINE</strong>: April 15</li><li>For arrival during the Spring Semester (January – May 15 ) - <strong>DEADLINE</strong>: September 15</li><li>For arrival during the summer (May 15 – August 15) - <strong>DEADLINE</strong>: January 15</li></ul><p>The application process, from acceptance as a visiting scholar until arrival in the U.S., often takes at least three months and can take up to six months to complete due to visa regulations. Scholars should plan their arrival date accordingly.</p><h4><strong><a name="Privileges"></a>Privileges and Responsibilities of a Visiting Scholar</strong></h4><p>ISAS Visiting Scholars are independent researchers while in residence at Berkeley. Visiting Scholars enjoy full access to Berkeley libraries and electronic resources and receive an e-mail account for use during their stay. They may be invited to present or otherwise take part in seminars or conferences organized by the ISAS. Visiting Scholars are welcome to attend all announced scholarly events on campus. Classroom participation as an auditor is subject to the approval of individual faculty members. All Visiting Scholars are asked to submit a final report on the outcome of their research affiliation. The ISAS appreciates copies of publications or papers completed during a visitor's affiliation with the Institute.</p><p>Please note that office space may be available on a first come, first served basis.</p><h4><strong><a name="Procedures"></a>Application Procedures</strong></h4><p>A complete application consists of:</p><table border="0" cellspacing="10" cellpadding="10"><tbody><tr style="background-color: #e0e0e0;"><td><p>A cover letter/letter of introduction (in English)</p></td></tr><tr style="background-color: #b4b4b4;"><td><p>A research proposal addressing the following:</p></td></tr><tr style="background-color: #e0e0e0;"><td><ul><li>Title of proposed project while in residence at Berkeley</li><li>Description of research project and plan of research</li><li>Research goals during period of affiliation</li><li>Brief statement on how affiliation with the Institute will help you accomplish these goals or further your career development</li><li>Proposed arrival date and length of stay</li></ul></td></tr><tr style="background-color: #b4b4b4;"><td><p>Name and contact information for Faculty Sponsor at UC Berkeley</p></td></tr><tr style="background-color: #e0e0e0;"><td><p>Curriculum vitae (in English)</p></td></tr><tr><td>&nbsp;</td></tr><tr style="background-color: #b4b4b4;"><td><p><strong>For International Visitors</strong> <strong>ONLY</strong></p></td></tr><tr style="background-color: #e0e0e0;"><td><p>Proof of Funding:</p></td></tr><tr style="background-color: #e0e0e0;"><td><ul><li>The Institute&nbsp;does not provide funding for visiting  scholars/researchers it agrees to host. Applicants must submit  documentation verifying and detailing funding for the entire period of  their desired affiliation. If funding documentation is not in English,  the applicant should provide a translation.</li><li>Note that minimum funding requirements for issuance of United States visa are as follows:<ul><li>Minimum $1,600 per month for scholar</li><li>Plus additional $500 per month for spouse</li><li>Plus additional $200 per month for dependent child</li></ul></li><li>Funding may come from any of the following sources or a combination of them:<ul><li>Scholar's  home institution — Requires letter of support which details amount of  funding, use of funds, and date to which funding is guaranteed</li><li>A  fellowship awarded by the applicant's home government or a recognized  international organization — Requires letter of support which details  amount of funding, use of funds, and date to which funding is guaranteed</li><li>Personal funds — Requires a bank statement or letter detailing the total amount in savings available</li></ul></li></ul></td></tr><tr style="background-color: #b4b4b4;"><td><p>Copy of passport information page for scholar and any accompanying dependents</p></td></tr><tr style="background-color: #e0e0e0;"><td><p>Once all fees have been paid and secondary application materials have been received, the&nbsp;<span style="font-size: 12px; line-height: 1.5em; background-color: #e0e0e0;">Institute</span><span style="font-size: 12px; line-height: 1.5em;">&nbsp;will process the applicant's DS-2019 which will allow him/her to go to the nearest U.S. Consulate or Embassy to apply for the J-1 (Visiting Scholar) visa.</span></p></td></tr><tr style="background-color: #b4b4b4;"><td><p>After receipt of the DS-2019 and related materials, applicants are required to pay a one-time U.S. government Homeland Security processing fee of $180. Instructions on how to pay this fee will be sent to applicants with the DS-2019 and may also be found at <a href="http://www.fmjfee.com">http://www.fmjfee.com</a>. Once this fee has been paid, applicants will then contact the local Consulate or Embassy to apply for the J-1 visa. To find the address, phone number, and business hours of the nearest Consulate or Embassy, please visit the U.S. Department of State website: <a href="http://travel.state.gov" title="http://travel.state.gov">http://travel.state.gov</a>. Usually an interview with the American authorities is required to secure the J-1 visa.</p></td></tr><tr><td><p><strong>Complete applications may be mailed or e-mailed directly to:</strong></p></td></tr><tr><td style="padding-left: 60px;"><span style="color: #333333; font-size: 12px; background-color: #ffffff;">Institute</span>&nbsp;for South Asia Studies<br> Visitng Scholar Program<br> 10 Stephens Hall (Rear Annex)<br> University of California, Berkeley<br> Berkeley, California 94720-2310<br><a href="mailto:csas@berkeley.edu">isas@berkeley.edu</a></td></tr></tbody></table><p>Completed applications are then reviewed by the ISAS Visiting Scholar Committee. Applicants will be notified of the Committee's decision in writing within a reasonable period of time.</p><p><strong><strong><a name="Fees"></a></strong></strong>Successful applicants will be asked to submit additional application forms and to pay the required non-refundable fees listed below:</p><table style="width: 600px;" border="0"><tbody><tr><td style="border: 1px solid #ffffff; background-color: #a09e9f;" colspan="2"><strong>Fees*</strong></td><td style="border: 1px solid #ffffff; background-color: #a09e9f;"><strong>Spring Semester</strong><br></td><td style="border: 1px solid #ffffff; background-color: #a09e9f;"><strong>Fall Semester</strong><br></td></tr><tr><td style="border: 1px solid #ffffff; background-color: #e4e3e4;" colspan="4"><a href="https://vspa.berkeley.edu/visiting-researcher-scholar" target="_blank">University Visiting Scholar Service Fee</a></td></tr><tr><td style="border: 1px solid #ffffff; background-color: #d3d1d2; text-align: right;" rowspan="2">Visiting Scholars</td><td style="border: 1px solid #ffffff; background-color: #d3d1d2;">1st Yr.</td><td style="border: 1px solid #ffffff; background-color: #d3d1d2;">$750</td><td style="border: 1px solid #ffffff; background-color: #d3d1d2;">$750</td></tr><tr><td style="border: 1px solid #ffffff; background-color: #d3d1d2;">2nd Yr</td><td style="border: 1px solid #ffffff; background-color: #d3d1d2;">$750</td><td style="border: 1px solid #ffffff; background-color: #d3d1d2;">$1500</td></tr><tr><td style="border: 1px solid #ffffff; background-color: #d3d1d2; text-align: right;" rowspan="2">Visiting Student Researchers</td><td style="border: 1px solid #ffffff; background-color: #d3d1d2;">1st Yr.</td><td style="border: 1px solid #ffffff; background-color: #d3d1d2;">$750</td><td style="border: 1px solid #ffffff; background-color: #d3d1d2;">$1000</td></tr><tr><td style="border: 1px solid #ffffff; background-color: #d3d1d2;">2nd Yr</td><td style="border: 1px solid #ffffff; background-color: #d3d1d2;">$750</td><td style="border: 1px solid #ffffff; background-color: #d3d1d2;">$2500</td></tr><tr><td style="border: 1px solid #ffffff; background-color: #e4e3e4;" colspan="2">ISAS Affiliation Fee*</td><td style="border: 1px solid #ffffff; background-color: #e4e3e4;">$1500</td><td style="border: 1px solid #ffffff; background-color: #e4e3e4;">$1500</td></tr><tr><td style="border: 1px solid #ffffff; background-color: #d3d1d2;" colspan="4"><em><strong>For International Visiting Scholars ONLY**</strong></em><br></td></tr><tr><td style="border: 1px solid #ffffff; background-color: #d3d1d2; text-align: right;" colspan="2">J1 Visa Duration</td><td style="border: 1px solid #ffffff; background-color: #d3d1d2;">Six months or longer</td><td style="border: 1px solid #ffffff; background-color: #d3d1d2;">Six months or less</td></tr><tr><td style="border: 1px solid #ffffff; background-color: #d3d1d2; text-align: right;" colspan="2">J1 Visa Extension</td><td style="border: 1px solid #ffffff; background-color: #d3d1d2;">Allowed</td><td style="border: 1px solid #ffffff; background-color: #d3d1d2;">Not Allowed</td></tr><tr><td style="border: 1px solid #ffffff; background-color: #d3d1d2; text-align: right;" colspan="2">J-1 Visa Processing Fee</td><td style="border: 1px solid #ffffff; background-color: #d3d1d2;">$540</td><td style="border: 1px solid #ffffff; background-color: #d3d1d2;">$540</td></tr><tr><td style="border: 1px solid #ffffff; background-color: #d3d1d2; text-align: right;" colspan="2">U.S. government Homeland Security processing Fee</td><td style="border: 1px solid #ffffff; background-color: #d3d1d2;">$180</td><td style="border: 1px solid #ffffff; background-color: #d3d1d2;">$180</td></tr></tbody></table><p><br>* Fees must be paid in US dollars and can be in the form of an international money order, cashier's check, or personal check payable to "UC Regents". <br>** These fees are in addition to the "Proof of Funding" required for the issuance of a J1 visa as described in the "Application Procedures" section above.</p><p>Once an invited Visiting Scholar has the visa in hand and travel plans scheduled, she/he should inform the&nbsp;<span style="font-size: 12px; background-color: #ffffff;">Institute</span>&nbsp;of her/his arrival dates and to schedule an appointment to complete the arrival forms required by the US government.</p><p>If you have specific questions regarding the ISAS Visiting Scholars Program, please e-mail <a href="mailto:isas@berkeley.edu">isas@berkeley.edu</a> or visit the following websites:</p><ul><li><a href="https://vspa.berkeley.edu/">Visiting Scholars and Postdoc Affairs</a></li><li><a href="http://internationaloffice.berkeley.edu/">Berkeley International Office</a></li></ul>  </div>

<table style="font-size: 15.2px; width: 730px;" border="0">
<tbody style="font-size: 15.2px;">
<tr style="font-size: 15.2px;">
<td style="background-color: #4b8b2f;"><span style="color: #ffffff;"><strong style="font-size: 12px;"><span style="font-size: medium;">ISLAM, YOUTH &amp; NEW MEDIA</span></strong></span></td>
</tr>
<tr style="font-size: 15.2px;">
<td style="background-color: #353535;">
<h3 style="font-size: 1.3em; line-height: 1.3em; margin-top: 0.769em; margin-bottom: 0.769em; background-color: #353535;">
<p style="color: #ffffff; font-family: Trebuchet, 'Trebuchet MS'; font-size: 13px; text-align: justify; margin-top: 1em; margin-bottom: 1em; line-height: 18.004px; background-color: #353535;"><img src="http://southasia.berkeley.edu/sites/default/files/shared/events/Islam_Today/Islam_Al_youm.png" width="237" height="121" style="float: right; margin-left: 10px;" />“Islam Today: New Media and Youth Culture in the Middle East, South Asia and Southeast Asia” is a new collaborative program being organized by UC Berkeley’s Centers for Middle Eastern Studies, South Asia Studies, and Southeast Asia Studies for 2009-2010.</p>
<p style="color: #ffffff; font-family: Trebuchet, 'Trebuchet MS'; font-size: 13px; text-align: justify; margin-top: 1em; margin-bottom: 1em; line-height: 18.004px; background-color: #353535;">This program, with funding support from the Social Science Research Council in New York, is designed generally to increase public understanding in the U.S. about Islam, by looking at how Muslim youth around the world are using new media to explore their identities, seek out and create "virtual" communities, and confront harmful anti-Muslim stereotypes, especially after the anti-Muslim backlash in the post 9/11 era.</p>
<p style="color: #ffffff; font-family: Trebuchet, 'Trebuchet MS'; font-size: 13px; text-align: justify; margin-top: 1em; margin-bottom: 1em; line-height: 18.004px; background-color: #353535;">This series of programs will bring together faculty, community organizations, activists, politicians, filmmakers, comedians, writers, musicians, private sector companies, bloggers, and young people active on social networking websites connected with Islam. Since the topic of discussion itself involves new media and culture, the issues raised through this program will be disseminated through these various mediums - blogs, websites, comedy routines, and popular writings - thus not only reaching a range of communities in the Bay Area but also the virtual communities connected with one another through online forums and networking.</p>
<p style="color: #ffffff; font-family: Trebuchet, 'Trebuchet MS'; font-size: 13px; text-align: justify; margin-top: 1em; margin-bottom: 1em; line-height: 18.004px; background-color: #353535;">Muslims from all parts of the world since 9/11 are facing discrimination and even threats of violence. For many young people, this post-9/11 world has sparked a new, if not confusing, relationship with their own identities as Muslims. While some young men and women may not have even identified themselves strongly as Muslim before 9/11, they have found that even just their last names may now trigger their being targeted, profiled, and even discriminated against. Others, who may have always had a close relationship to Islam and Islamic practices, have been suddenly forced to defend their religion to those who brand all Muslims as terrorists. These difficult times have led young Muslims all over the world to try and find answers, connect with other individuals in similar situations, debate issues, and even subvert commonly held notions of Islam.</p>
<p style="color: #ffffff; font-family: Trebuchet, 'Trebuchet MS'; font-size: 13px; text-align: justify; margin-top: 1em; margin-bottom: 1em; line-height: 18.004px; background-color: #353535;">The ability to use the media for "networking" has been significant for these youth, as many have often felt isolated and have come to find solace in these virtual communities. As one young Muslim said, "Young Muslims are ‘resorting to this virtual world because we have no space in the actual world...'" The creation of community through media and the subversion of stereotypes through popular culture, including comedy, comic books, film, and music, have all allowed for this new generation of Muslim youth to develop their own identity. At the same time, the clash between traditional and modern forms of religious practice and ideals is continually being played out in these different forums. The ultimate goal for many young Muslims who use new media or youth culture as forms of expression are to change negative opinions and dispel stereotypes.</p>
<p style="color: #ffffff; font-family: Trebuchet, 'Trebuchet MS'; font-size: 13px; text-align: justify; margin-top: 1em; margin-bottom: 1em; line-height: 18.004px; background-color: #353535;">As technology continues to evolve, including the means to connect and communicate in cyberspace, and as the countries of these three regions grapple with the changes wrought by modernization and by the effects of changing patterns in political alignments, young Muslims should see ever more opportunities to make themselves heard. What this emergence of new voices may suggest for the future of Islam, for the futures of their home countries, and for the U.S. itself, needs to be explored.</p>
<p style="color: #ffffff; font-family: Trebuchet, 'Trebuchet MS'; font-size: 13px; text-align: justify; margin-top: 1em; margin-bottom: 1em; line-height: 18.004px; background-color: #353535;">We are organizing three events as part of this program. They are:</p>
<p style="color: #ffffff; font-family: Trebuchet, 'Trebuchet MS'; font-size: 13px; text-align: justify; margin-top: 1em; margin-bottom: 1em; line-height: 18.004px; background-color: #353535;">Youth, New Media &amp; Politics in the Muslim World: Our first forum will focus on how Muslim youth are using various forms of new media as a way to network with like-minded individuals, find answers to difficult questions, and challenge commonly held attitudes and stereotypes about Islam, particularly in the post 9/11 era.</p>
<p style="color: #ffffff; font-family: Trebuchet, 'Trebuchet MS'; font-size: 13px; text-align: justify; margin-top: 1em; margin-bottom: 1em; line-height: 18.004px; background-color: #353535;">Youth and New forms of Social Networking: Networking has been significant for these youth, as many who feel isolated have come to find solace in these virtual communities, as well as a place where they establish their own presence and express themselves.Our second forum will explore the ways in which young Muslims use the media for creating virtual communities.</p>
<p style="color: #ffffff; font-family: Trebuchet, 'Trebuchet MS'; font-size: 13px; text-align: justify; margin-top: 1em; margin-bottom: 1em; line-height: 18.004px; background-color: #353535;">Festival on Youth, Islam and the Arts: This festival will involve a series of events designed to focus on Muslim youth and some of the forms of popular culture and expression that are being used to establish a new Muslim identity and change negative attitudes. The last few years have witnessed a rise in comedians, music groups, and filmmakers exploring the struggles Muslims have been facing around the world since 9/11 and examining commonly held beliefs about Islam. Young people are using these various mediums to creatively and subtly challenge perceptions and ideas.</p>
</h3>
</td>
</tr>
</tbody>
</table>
  </div>

  
  </div>
  </div>
</div>
  </div>
</div>
</div></div>

<div class="panel-pane pane-node"  id="right_top_secondary">
  
  
  
  <div class="pane-content">
    <div id="node-90" class="node clear-block">


  <h2><a href="/rawmaintop" title=""></a></h2>

  <div class="meta">
  
    </div>

  <div class="content">
    <!--
--><!--
--><p><img id="top_bkground" src="http://southasia.berkeley.edu/sites/default/files/shared/img/SEC-strip.png" /></p>
<div id="strip">
<div id="secondary_menu"><a href="/about-us">ABOUT</a> | <a href="/mailing-list">JOIN</a> | <a href="/contactsdirections">CONTACT</a> | <a href="give-big-south-asia">SUPPORT</a> | <a href="https://www.facebook.com/pages/Center-for-South-Asia-Studies/76502306608"><img id="facebook_icon" src="/sites/default/files/shared/img/facebook.png" alt="facebook logo" width="25" height="25" align="absmiddle" /></a> &nbsp;</div>
</div>
<!--end strip --><!--end strip -->  </div>

</div>  </div>

  
  </div>
<div class="panel-region-separator"></div><div class="panel-pane pane-node-title"  id="page_title">
  
  
  
  <div class="pane-content">
    Language Programs  </div>

  
  </div>
<div class="panel-region-separator"></div><div class="panel-pane pane-node-body"  id="secondary_page_main">
  
  
  
  <div class="pane-content">
    <p>Berkeley provides comprehensive language instruction at three levels, from introductory to advanced, in eight of the major literary and spoken languages of five countries in South Asia: Hindi, Urdu, Tamil, Bengali, Punjabi, Sanskrit, Tibetan and the recently added Telugu. Enrollments in South Asian languages are substantial and have been steadily growing in&nbsp;recent years. We have been able to offer language instruction in these languages because of demand from the student body and overwhelming support from the Bengali, Punjabi, Tamil and Telugu speaking communities.</p><p>Our language lecturers — <a href="/sally-j-sutherland-goldman" target="_blank">Sally J. Sutherland Goldman</a> (Sanskrit), <a href="http://southasia.berkeley.edu/usha-jain" target="_blank">Usha Jain</a> (Hindi),&nbsp;<a href="http://southasia.berkeley.edu/upkar-k-ubhi" target="_blank">Upkar K. Ubhi</a> (Punjabi), <a href="http://southasia.berkeley.edu/gregory-maxwell-bruce" target="_blank">Gregory Maxwell Bruce</a> (Urdu), <a href="http://southasia.berkeley.edu/amitabha-basu" target="_blank">Amitabha Basu</a> (Bangla), <a href="http://southasia.berkeley.edu/s-bharathy" target="_blank">S. Bharathy </a>(Tamil &amp; Telugu) and <a href="http://buddhiststudies.berkeley.edu/people/lecturer_profiles.html#sparham" target="_blank">Gareth Sparham</a> (Tibetan)—provide language training and expertise across South Asian literary traditions, from modern conversational language classes to the reading of classical texts.</p><table border="0"><tbody><tr><td class="table_background">&nbsp;</td><td class="table_background">&nbsp;</td><td class="table_background">&nbsp;</td><td class="table_background">&nbsp;</td><td class="table_background">&nbsp;</td><td class="table_background">&nbsp;</td><td style="text-align: center;"><p><a href="http://southasia.berkeley.edu/bangla"><img href="http://southasia.berkeley.edu/urdu"><strong>Urdu</strong></a></strong></td><td class="table_background">&nbsp;</td></tr><tr><td class="table_background">&nbsp;</td><td class="table_background">&nbsp;</td><td class="table_background">&nbsp;</td><td class="table_background">&nbsp;</td><td class="table_background">&nbsp;</td><td class="table_background">&nbsp;</td><td class="table_background">&nbsp;</td><td class="table_background">&nbsp;</td><td class="table_background">&nbsp;</td></tr></tbody></table><h3><strong>Language Publications</strong></h3> <p>One measure of the quality of the language program is certainly the fact that the three lecturers in Hindi (<a href="http://southasia.berkeley.edu/usha-jain">Usha Jain</a>), Tamil (<a href="http://southasia.berkeley.edu/kausalya-hart">Kausalya Hart</a>) and Sanskrit (<a href="/sally-j-sutherland-goldman">Sally J Sutherland. Goldman</a> with <a href="/robert-goldman">Robert Goldman</a>) have written the definitive textbooks for the teaching of their respective languages in North America. ISAS’ publishing program publishes all these books. For further information and buying information please go to our <a href="/csas-language-publications">ISAS Language Publications page</a><strong>.</strong></p><table style="height: 162px;" border="0"><tbody><tr><td class="table_background"><p style="text-align: center;"><img src="sites/default/files/shared/Beg20Hindi20Grammar.png" alt="Beginner Hindi" title="Beginner Hindi" width="50" height="73"></p></td><td>&nbsp;</td><td class="table_background"><p style="text-align: center;"><img src="sites/default/files/shared/Inter20Hindi20Grammar.png" alt="Inter Hindi" title="Inter Hindi" width="50" height="73"></p></td><td>&nbsp;</td><td class="table_background"><p style="text-align: center;"><img src="sites/default/files/shared/Adv20Hindi20Grammar.png" alt="Adv Hindi" title="Adv Hindi" width="50" height="73"></p></td><td>&nbsp;</td><td class="table_background"><p style="text-align: center;"><img src="sites/default/files/shared/Tamil20for20Begin.png" width="50" height="73"></p></td><td>&nbsp;</td><td class="table_background"><p style="text-align: center;"><img src="sites/default/files/shared/Sanskrit.png" alt="Sanskrit book" title="Sanskrit book" width="50" height="73"></p></td></tr><tr style="text-align: center;"><td style="text-align: center;"><strong>Introduction to<br>Hindi Grammar</strong></td><td>&nbsp;</td><td style="text-align: center;"><strong>Intermediate<br>Hindi Reader<br></strong></td><td><strong>&nbsp;</strong></td><td><strong>Advanced<br>Hindi Grammar <br></strong></td><td>&nbsp;</td><td><strong>Tamil for<br>Beginners </strong><br></td><td>&nbsp;</td><td>&nbsp;<strong>Devavanipravesika<br>An Intro to Sanskrit</strong><br></td></tr></tbody></table><p><img src="/sites/default/files/resize/shared/South20Southeast20Asia20Library-226x201.jpg" alt="SSEAL LIb" title="SSEAL LIb" width="226" height="201" style="float: right; border: 15px solid white; margin-top: 5px; margin-bottom: 5px;" /></p> <h3 style="text-align: left;"><strong>South Asia Related Library Holdings<br></strong></h3> <div><p style="text-align: justify;">Berkeley’s South Asia collection ranks among the four leading South Asia collections in the nation.</p><p style="text-align: justify;">The South Asia Library boasts the following holdings: Subscriptions for about 5,300 serials, 1,750 of which are published in regional languages; 25 journals and newspapers from the South Asia diasporic community; 25 South Asia daily newspapers;<span style="font-size: 12px; line-height: 1.5em;">more than 450,000 monographs, with around 10,000 new volumes added annually; 3,700 maps; 600 videos and DVDs; numerous special collections thematically or linguistically arranged; extensive special format holdings, such as films, prints, sound recordings, slides and a number of palm leaf manuscripts in Tamil, Sanskrit and Sinhala.</span></p><table border="0"><tbody><tr><td class="table_background" style="text-align: center;"><strong>For further information on each of these language programs please browse through the menu items on the left.</strong></td></tr></tbody></table></div>  </div>

  
  </div>
  </div>
</div>
  </div>
</div>

    <div id="node-90" class="node clear-block">


  <h2><a href="/rawmaintop" title=""></a></h2>

  <div class="meta">
  
    </div>

  <div class="content">
    <!--
--><!--
--><p><img id="top_bkground" src="http://southasia.berkeley.edu/sites/default/files/shared/img/SEC-strip.png" /></p>
<div id="strip">
<div id="secondary_menu"><a href="/about-us">ABOUT</a> | <a href="/mailing-list">JOIN</a> | <a href="/contactsdirections">CONTACT</a> | <a href="give-big-south-asia">SUPPORT</a> | <a href="https://www.facebook.com/pages/Center-for-South-Asia-Studies/76502306608"><img id="facebook_icon" src="/sites/default/files/shared/img/facebook.png" alt="facebook logo" width="25" height="25" align="absmiddle" /></a> &nbsp;</div>
